  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_3e9b23c1-4da2-4237-963b-0b71d0edb615'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText11142784376399699723" style="display:none"><b>An aristocratic French family, a legendary château, and buried secrets with the power to destroy two generations torn between duty and desire.</b><br /><br />La Côte d’Azur, 1998: In the sun-dappled south of France, Emilie de la Martinières, the last of her gilded line, inherits her childhood home, a magnificent château and vineyard. With the property comes a mountain of debt—and almost as many questions . . .<br /><br />Paris, 1944: A bright, young British office clerk, Constance Carruthers, is sent undercover to Paris to be part of Churchill’s Special Operations Executive during the climax of the Nazi occupation. Separated from her contacts in the Resistance, she soon stumbles into the heart of a prominent family who regularly entertain elite members of the German military even as they plot to liberate France. But in a city rife with collaborators and rebels, Constance’s most difficult decision may be determining whom to trust with her heart.<br /><br />As Emilie discovers what really happened to her family during the war and finds a connection to Constance much closer than she suspects, the château itself may provide the clues that unlock the mysteries of her past, present, and future. Here is a dazzling novel of intrigue and passion from one of the world’s most beloved storytellers.<br /><br />Note to readers: In the UK, this book is published under the title <i>The Light Behind the Window.</i></span>

<div id="review_420320668" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/420320668" />
    <a title="Marguerite Kaye" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3578169-marguerite-kaye"><img alt="Marguerite Kaye" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578321599p2/3578169.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/420320668?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marguerite Kaye" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marguerite Kaye" href="/user/show/3578169-marguerite-kaye">Marguerite Kaye</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781447218425" href="/book/show/15718885-the-light-behind-the-window">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer420320668" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5395549309511246853">If I can't give a book an honest 3 stars, it hasn't worked for me. I don't rate them 1 or 2 because I personally think this gives people a false picture, but I do try and explain. So it was with this on. <br/><br/>The Light Behind the Window was the kind of book I like. Two stories linked, two timescales, and a bit of war - in this case, WWII. The thing is, I read it very quickly, and it's not a short book, but it was sort of a couldn't-put-down book. The problem was that the reason I couldn't put it down</span>
  <span id="freeText5395549309511246853" style="display:none">If I can't give a book an honest 3 stars, it hasn't worked for me. I don't rate them 1 or 2 because I personally think this gives people a false picture, but I do try and explain. So it was with this on. <br /><br />The Light Behind the Window was the kind of book I like. Two stories linked, two timescales, and a bit of war - in this case, WWII. The thing is, I read it very quickly, and it's not a short book, but it was sort of a couldn't-put-down book. The problem was that the reason I couldn't put it down was not really because I wanted to know what would happen, it was to find out whether what I was right in what I predicted would happen right from the start. And sadly, in almost every aspect of the plot, I was right. <br /><br />And this is what was at the heart of what didn't work for me. This book was simply way too predictable. It had so many coincidences and connections it was worthy of Dickens, and though some of them weren't way off, they felt it. Instead of that nice feeling you get when a plot turns a corner and all is revealed, what I felt was right, told you so. <br /><br />But predictability of plot can be okay if you are interested in the characters. Which was my second issue. In particulare Emilie, the main protagonist in the modern-day story, drove me mad. She is the daughter of an aristocratic family, whose socialite mother was totally uninterested in her. The mother dies at the start and Emilie, who has 'rebelled' by abandoning the social life and becoming a vet, is left with a huge chateau on her hands. You'd think someone who has worked hard enough and single-mindedly enough to have such a career would have a bit of gumption, but Emilie seemed to me to have absolutely none. She dithers and she swithers. When her mother's dog is run over, she actually has to consult another vet! She seems to think she can only practice in Paris, and that any move to any other part or France or any other country must mean she gives up her career (the one she's worked so hard to succeed at) and frankly, when she met her Nemesis (and anyone but Emilie would have known right from the start that's what he was) I thought she deserved all she got. <br /><br />There were lots of sub-plots in this book I'd have liked under other circumstances, but I just couldn't get past Emilie. Yet, as I said at the start, I didn't put it down either. Which means it must have pulling power. So maybe it's just me. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5395549309511246853" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_654178876" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/654178876" />
    <a title="Elizabeth of Silver&#39;s Reviews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1882027-elizabeth-of-silver-s-reviews"><img alt="Elizabeth of Silver&#39;s Reviews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1297997409p2/1882027.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/654178876?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elizabeth of Silver&#39;s Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elizabeth of Silver&#39;s Reviews" href="/user/show/1882027-elizabeth-of-silver-s-reviews">Elizabeth of Silver&#39;s Reviews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer654178876" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3668024185906949343">Castles, hidden rooms, families, World War II, and history coming alive as past and present blend together for an incredible, marvelously detailed read. <br/> <br/>Emilie de la Martinieres is the sole surviving member of her family and is left with a chateau with vineyards and another home in Paris. Both homes are filled with memories and contents worth millions. But, the millions won't be Emile's because of the debt her mother mounted over the years. Emilie needs to decide if she should sell or keep the </span>
  <span id="freeText3668024185906949343" style="display:none">Castles, hidden rooms, families, World War II, and history coming alive as past and present blend together for an incredible, marvelously detailed read. <br /> <br />Emilie de la Martinieres is the sole surviving member of her family and is left with a chateau with vineyards and another home in Paris. Both homes are filled with memories and contents worth millions. But, the millions won't be Emile's because of the debt her mother mounted over the years. Emilie needs to decide if she should sell or keep the chateau. She never had to deal with finances and was doing it alone until a complete stranger, Sebastian, came on the scene.<br /><br />Sebastian's family had some connection to Emilie's chateau and vineyard, and the winemakers on the estate knew what that connection was. The account of the important family connection is revealed through Constance's life during WWII and her connection to the de la Martinieries' family. But, did Sebastian suddenly appear and help Emilie because of the family connection or because he was interested in the valuable paintings inside her estates and most of all her family inheritance?<br /><br />THE LAVENDER GARDEN moves back and forth from current day to WWII making a beautiful story even more enticing. The WWII details were fascinating and very well researched.<br /><br />The detailed descriptions of the castle, the French society during WWII, the hint of mystery about the de la Martinieries' history, and the current-day love story make this book another amazing, mesmerizing, and fantastic Lucinda Riley novel. <br /> <br />THE LAVENDER GARDEN had wonderful characters that were believable as well as characters that you would want to share a day with. Being in a beautiful chateau with a vineyard, being in Paris and a small French village, being in an English castle, and being with characters you definitely will bond with made the book even more appealing. <br /><br />This is by far my favorite Lucinda Riley book. I loved her detail about the French and English countryside and absolutely loved the specifics of the ancestry of Emilee's family. Digging into a family's history is my favorite historical thing to do. The ending is wonderful.<br /><br />I hope you get to read it. 5/5<br /><br />This book was given to me free of charge and without compensation in return for an honest review. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3668024185906949343" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_454877373" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/454877373" />
    <a title="Anna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1632609-anna"><img alt="Anna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307368032p2/1632609.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/454877373?book_show_action=true">Nov 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anna" href="/user/show/1632609-anna">Anna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781447218425" href="/book/show/15718885-the-light-behind-the-window">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1632609-anna?shelf=world-war-two">world-war-two</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1632609-anna?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1632609-anna?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1632609-anna?shelf=dual-timeline">dual-timeline</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1632609-anna?shelf=france-italy-spain">france-italy-spain</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer454877373" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7790752895044879448">This is my third Lucinda Riley book. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11973190.The_Girl_on_the_Cliff' title='The Girl on the Cliff by Lucinda Riley' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Girl on the Cliff</a> was a big hit, but <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12449167.The_Orchid_House' title='The Orchid House by Lucinda Riley' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Orchid House</a> was a meandering miss, and after the first few chapters I thought <i>The Light Behind The Window</i> would be heading for another miss too. It has a very slow and simplistic beginning, including my dialogue dislike of over-using names even when only two people are talking to each other. Argh. However, when the 'story proper' finally kicked in I became hooked despite my niggles. <br/><br/>In present day France, Emilie i</span>
  <span id="freeText7790752895044879448" style="display:none">This is my third Lucinda Riley book. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11973190.The_Girl_on_the_Cliff" title="The Girl on the Cliff by Lucinda Riley" rel="nofollow noopener">The Girl on the Cliff</a> was a big hit, but <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12449167.The_Orchid_House" title="The Orchid House by Lucinda Riley" rel="nofollow noopener">The Orchid House</a> was a meandering miss, and after the first few chapters I thought <i>The Light Behind The Window</i> would be heading for another miss too. It has a very slow and simplistic beginning, including my dialogue dislike of over-using names even when only two people are talking to each other. Argh. However, when the 'story proper' finally kicked in I became hooked despite my niggles. <br /><br />In present day France, Emilie inherits her parents' old crumbling château. She meets Englishman Sebastian who says that his grandmother, Constance, knew her father, Edouard, during WW2. We then travel back to war-torn London where Connie is enrolled as a Special Operations Executive and dropped into occupied France to assist the Allies and the Resistance. Things don't go according to plan, and she instead finds herself caught up in liberator Edouard's dangerous game of deception involving his beautiful sister Sophia and a pair of high ranking German officer brothers. <br /><br />The incredible bravery of the SOE, the Resistance and the ordinary French men and women is movingly told; I'm a Brit used to war stories told from home soil and am ashamed to say how little I know about day to day occupied France. That's not to say this is a gritty war book though, far from it. There are some tense moments, but they're dealt with 'nicely' with only hints of the horrors that happen off-screen. The main body of this book is how the long-lost secrets of the past affect the future generations.<br /><br />As with most dual-timeline books, the present-day story wasn't a patch on the past, but the bittersweet wartime story of loyalty and sacrifice more than made up for any shortcomings with its many twists and turns (just when you think you have it all figured out....) and an emotional ending which had me reaching for the tissues. Not a complete hit, but still a very decent read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7790752895044879448" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_874655684" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/874655684" />
    <a title="Ana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21872732-ana"><img alt="Ana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1447688664p2/21872732.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/874655684?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ana" href="/user/show/21872732-ana">Ana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer874655684" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12242100312640107172">This book sounded so promising but it was rather disappointing and bland. The plot was okay, but very slow-moving at times and the ending was very predictable to me. My biggest issue was the unnecessary time the author spent on 'pleasant' conversations; i'm sure if someone checked which words were the most used one's in this book, 'thank you' would win. All the characters talk and interact with each other but in reality they're not saying anything. It felt like I read the same conversation over </span>
  <span id="freeText12242100312640107172" style="display:none">This book sounded so promising but it was rather disappointing and bland. The plot was okay, but very slow-moving at times and the ending was very predictable to me. My biggest issue was the unnecessary time the author spent on 'pleasant' conversations; i'm sure if someone checked which words were the most used one's in this book, 'thank you' would win. All the characters talk and interact with each other but in reality they're not saying anything. It felt like I read the same conversation over and over again, there was no differentiating between characters; they all seem to posses the same speech pattern and the same way of articulation, even a 13 year old compared with an 80+ year old. You can barely see any sort of personality except for a few traits and even with those the authors seems to feel the need to divide the characters either into 'bad' or 'good'. The good one's seem to have no fault and the bad one's have no redeeming qualities whatsoever, which makes it hard to take the characters seriously, considering people just aren't like that.<br /><br />The characters don't seem to react to certain things like normal people would. [spoilers ahead] When Emilie paints the room yellow and Alex provokes her a bit, she runs away, locks herself away in her room, cries and labels him 'Monster', yet when she finds out that Sebastian has been betraying her all along, she barely reacts to it. Same with the boy, his mother dies but he is basically only caring about moving in with Emilie and a year later he seems to be perfectly okay. Or Connie not reacting to being raped at all, she just brushes it aside. Or the fact that Sophia died, she seemed pretty indifferent to it for the most part. They just don't come across as genuine characters.<br /><br />This book is over 500 pages long with at least 2/3 of it being waste that doesn't serve to move the plot along, yet the ending was completely rushed. Very poorly executed, in my opinion. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12242100312640107172" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1119396082" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1119396082" />
    <a title="Idril Celebrindal" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3527964-idril-celebrindal"><img alt="Idril Celebrindal" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457372997p2/3527964.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1119396082?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Idril Celebrindal" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Idril Celebrindal" href="/user/show/3527964-idril-celebrindal">Idril Celebrindal</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1119396082" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3929608260965983884">I have been having really bad luck with my reading choices lately. I don't understand why so many people seem to want to write books about women in SOE that in fact aren't about what women in SOE did. Or at least, I thought this would be about a woman in SOE (along with a related story set in the more or less present day), but apparently it wanted to be a soapy drama. Which could have been okay, except that it was so clunky and flat.<br/><br/>I know this is fiction and heaven knows I am not a very big fan</span>
  <span id="freeText3929608260965983884" style="display:none">I have been having really bad luck with my reading choices lately. I don't understand why so many people seem to want to write books about women in SOE that in fact aren't about what women in SOE did. Or at least, I thought this would be about a woman in SOE (along with a related story set in the more or less present day), but apparently it wanted to be a soapy drama. Which could have been okay, except that it was so clunky and flat.<br /><br />I know this is fiction and heaven knows I am not a very big fan of "gritty" realism, but there does have to be <i>some</i> detail to evoke a sense of reality and place. I can't find any of that here. The author tosses in a few names of some actual people from SOE, but that's where it stops. <br /><br />Did you know that in France, coffee was available throughout the entirety of WW2? You didn't, really? Of course you didn't, because that is most amateur mistake I've ever seen. "But, Idril," you say, "Edouard was rich and bought things on the black market." Okay, fine; that doesn't really work because the black market wasn't just a place you could swan into and pick up whatever you liked, so even then there would still be shortages and I imagine you'd want to save what you did find for the dangerous Nazis who think you are on their side and need to be pampered, but fine. However, in this book <i>everyone</i> has coffee. Wander into a cafe in occupied Paris, grab some coffee; stop at a rural train station, sip some coffee; hide in a basement and warm up with some coffee!<br /><br />"Idril," you say, "I think you need to calm down."<br /><br />You may be right. It's only coffee. So let's also talk about forged identity papers. Based on this book I'd assume 90% of citizens in France during the war had forged papers. Need new papers? Your local aristocrat can have them whipped up overnight! Don't know any aristocrats? Head to the nearest cottage; the peasantry can meet the same deadline for half the price! (I am assuming on the price thing; money is never mentioned and it's never hard for anyone to obtain anything in this book.)<br /><br />Air raids are boring to sit through apparently but don't damage anything, apparently, and travel is smellier but apparently everyone does it. Cousins from Vichy France apparently head to Paris for holidays without any difficulty. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[A few month after the war Constance wants to go home so she just does, without difficulty. In reality it took people months to find passage home. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Constance is (supposedly) trained by SOE but as soon as she gets to France she can't be involved with SOE contacts in any way. Or do anything. Except drink coffee.<br /><br />If you don't care what life was like in wartime France, the hardships and dangers, why bother to set your story there? With one exception nothing really difficult happens to these ridiculous characters. And they are so ridiculous. They do nothing and then talk to each other about how brave they all are.<br /><br />As for the modern part of the novel, "naive woman falls for charming man, whom the reader suspects is bad news" could be an interesting story. But in this, Sebastian is so obviously full of shit and so bland, and Emilie is so bland and seems so stupid for falling for it, that I just felt bored waiting for the inevitable revelation. And here again was a total lack of challenge for the characters: the first chapter tells us Emilie's mother spent all the family fortune and who knows what will happen to the family chateau and sacre bleu! Oh, but, just sell the town house and some jewelry and you're not only set for life but can carry out expensive renovations and write your husband checks for multiple tens of thousands of pounds without blinking.<br /><br />And the husband: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Still can't figure out why he married her. I mean, if it was just "her money" that'd be one thing. But we're told it was to steal a specific book. For money. But the book isn't really THAT valuable, comparatively. I mean, it's a ton of money to me, but in context it isn't. I don't think so, anyway, because our novel isn't actually sure how much this MacGuffin is worth. It's not even the most valuable book in the chateau's library. There were plenty of other objects he could have stolen, since Emilie didn't even know what she owned. The book trots this "steal one specific book" explanation out at the end and even tries to lampshade it but it just doesn't make sense. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />But the crowning idiocy is at the convergence of the two stories: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[After the war ends what on earth is the justification for not telling Frederik about his daughter?! And he just doesn't care! "You lied to me about <i>my child</i> for 55 years and only told me she existed <i>after she died</i> so I had no hope of ever having a relationship with her, but hey, water under the bridge!" And Emilie and Jean congratulate Jacques on how wise this decision was. (?!) It was baffling and silly and nonsensical. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I mean, I gave it two stars because I did read the whole thing (for some unknown reason). I feel like lately I've been writing only flippantly dismissive reviews of books I suffered through, which is getting tiresome. I'd really like to read something I enjoy. This was not it.<br /><br />As a final note, my favorite part was the actual <a href="http://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Main/BigNo" rel="nofollow noopener">Big No</a> set out ridiculously in type.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3929608260965983884" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14466802006073156605">I had a difficult time getting into this novel. The relationship that forms between two of the main characters seemed artificial and contrived. For the first 60 pages, I just kept thinking, "how could Riley write such unconvincing dribble!" As it turns out, there was a method in her madness and it all came together later in the novel. Once I became immersed in the story, I got swept away in what is now the familiar intricacies of Riley's plots. While I liked The Orchid House and The Girl on the </span>
  <span id="freeText14466802006073156605" style="display:none">I had a difficult time getting into this novel. The relationship that forms between two of the main characters seemed artificial and contrived. For the first 60 pages, I just kept thinking, "how could Riley write such unconvincing dribble!" As it turns out, there was a method in her madness and it all came together later in the novel. Once I became immersed in the story, I got swept away in what is now the familiar intricacies of Riley's plots. While I liked The Orchid House and The Girl on the Cliff better than The Lavender Garden, this was still an entertaining and exciting story. I especially liked how it focused on women's roles in the underground resistance in France in WWII. This is a part of the war that I was not familiar with and I enjoyed learning about it. </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2488381966" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2488381966" />
    <a title="Hannah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6940509-hannah"><img alt="Hannah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1564833262p2/6940509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2488381966?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah" href="/user/show/6940509-hannah">Hannah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2488381966" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12528319572930815741"><b>1 Star</b> - Just horrible <br/><br/>TW; rape (I put it in one of the spoilers, but just in case someone wants to go through and read them all.)<br/><br/>I bought this book at a library book sale. I’d never heard of the book before, it wasn’t on my radar, however the description on the back of the book sounded interesting so I spent the 50¢ and bought it. I’ll boldly say it’s not even worth the half-dollar I paid for it. <br/><br/>This one is classified as historical fiction and that it is. I have no qualms with that. However, t</span>
  <span id="freeText12528319572930815741" style="display:none"><b>1 Star</b> - Just horrible <br /><br />TW; rape (I put it in one of the spoilers, but just in case someone wants to go through and read them all.)<br /><br />I bought this book at a library book sale. I’d never heard of the book before, it wasn’t on my radar, however the description on the back of the book sounded interesting so I spent the 50¢ and bought it. I’ll boldly say it’s not even worth the half-dollar I paid for it. <br /><br />This one is classified as historical fiction and that it is. I have no qualms with that. However, that’s probably my only non-objection to this one. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4512899.Lucinda_Riley" title="Lucinda Riley" rel="nofollow noopener">Lucinda Riley</a> attempts to interweave the stories of Emilie de la Martinières, a young French woman who recently inherited a vast fortune after her mother’s death, and Constance Carruthers, a young English woman who was sent to France during World War II as a special operative. Riley then tells the reader how these two women, decades apart, are intertwined. The potential this story had was immense but unfortunately it remains just that - potential. <br /><br />One of the first issues I stumbled across in this book is that it is so filled with clichés and overused tropes. They make the book truly unbearable. Only 20 pages in and I found the following: daughter hates mom but loves her dad, mom disapproves of daughter’s lifestyle, basic and stupid French stereotypes (foofy little dog, obsession with wine, aristocracy, etc.). I mean, fine, have one or two but not all of them, C’mon. <br /><br />I will also say that the dialogue and language in which this book is written is ridiculous. It’s kitschy in the WWII sections for sure and, throughout the whole book and both times periods, way too formal. I understand that for most of the book the characters are speaking in French but, as someone who speaks French, I also know how to translate it to English. The tone was just all wrong and way too off-putting. <br /><br />Now onto the characters. I don’t know if I’ve ever read a book with such one-dimensional and predictable characters. They seem like caricatures of themselves. It was so bizarre and not fun to read. I knew how each would react to a situation because none of them had any depth. Don’t misunderstand me, the author adds what she thinks is complexity to most of the characters but it doesn’t work. It falls flat on all counts. Take for instance Emilie, our 1990s “heroine.” From the first few pages the author sets her up to be a woman who’s rebelled against her family’s (mainly mother’s) wishes and taken an ordinary career - a vet. However, there is nothing rebellious or remotely interesting about her that sets her apart from what the reader can imagine to be her aristocratic counterparts. She’s incapable of doing anything on her own. Simply put, she is an idiot. That may sound harsh but it’s true. She is irritating and is so easily persuaded. Her reaction to Sebastian’s story about his brother, Alex, is horrifying. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Before we learn that basically everything Sebastian told Emilie is a lie, or very much misconstrued, she has no right to react to Alex the way she does. Don’t get me wrong, I’m not condoning drug use but why is that so scary? Maybe I’m being unfair (I probably am) but lord does she appear to be vapid. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The relationship between Emilie and Sebastian starts out on a creepy, weird note and that never bodes well. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[We quickly get a dreadful proposal scene. Sebastian, for anyone with a brain, is a no-go even before the proposal. But then we get that scene to confirm it. He gets angry with Emilie and it’s just a whole mess. Shoulda said no. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Their whole relationship is manipulative and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[fucked up <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. It has strong tendencies toward emotional and verbal abuse, maybe even financial if you stretch your mind a bit. They’re not a convincing couple at any point.<br /><br />I know I’ve focused on Emilie’s side of the story but much of the complaints I have for her storyline carry over to Constance’s. A unique grievance I have with her story is the <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ rape and assault she sustained. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> In general I don’t have issues when books <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[delve into rape and sexual assault but the problem here is that the author doesn’t dive into it. Constance is brutally assaulted and then we read about it twice more. We don’t get to see how she dealt with, even if that means she kept pushing feelings away. There are maybe two or three other mentions of it and then it just disappears. That creates a poor standard for how authors and readers should interact with such a serious topic. To give the author credit, the assault scene is written fine. I take issue with the aftermath. If you’re going to include something that serious, you need to include how the character deals with it because those acts have long-lasting consequences. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Just one other thing before I wrap this one up. The way Emilie throws in at the very end that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[she can’t have kids <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> feels rushed and makes zero sense. It doesn’t add anything to the story. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Yes, there’s Anton but that storyline could’ve happened without her whole melt down. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I just personally think that that scene was random and poorly done.<br /><br />Do I recommend this one? Absolutely not.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12528319572930815741" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_367710415" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/367710415" />
    <a title="Joanne D&#39;Arcy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3430550-joanne-d-arcy"><img alt="Joanne D&#39;Arcy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1268465284p2/3430550.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/367710415?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joanne D&#39;Arcy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joanne D&#39;Arcy" href="/user/show/3430550-joanne-d-arcy">Joanne D&#39;Arcy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781447218425" href="/book/show/15718885-the-light-behind-the-window">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer367710415" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer627403908178256091">Yet again Lucinda Riley has created and weaved a story which has you gripped from the beginning to the end. You have to keep reading, you have to know what happens you have to know if love will conquer all, if war will end, if all wrongs will be righted and that the light will shine again from behind the window where it has been hiding for many years of the main characters.<br/><br/>Emilie de la Martinieres is there when her glamorous mother draws her final breath. As the end comes, Emilie realises what a</span>
  <span id="freeText627403908178256091" style="display:none">Yet again Lucinda Riley has created and weaved a story which has you gripped from the beginning to the end. You have to keep reading, you have to know what happens you have to know if love will conquer all, if war will end, if all wrongs will be righted and that the light will shine again from behind the window where it has been hiding for many years of the main characters.<br /><br />Emilie de la Martinieres is there when her glamorous mother draws her final breath. As the end comes, Emilie realises what a task she now has to face, as the sole remaining heir she has to sort a flat in Paris, her mother's jewels and other remnants of her famous and glamorous life as well as the Chateau in the south of France, which her mother hated, but Emilie loved as a child when her father was alive.<br /><br />The Chateau holds memories good and bad, and as Emilie discovers these she also discovers something of the past which has an immediate effect on the future. The reader goes on an emotional rollercoaster with Emilie, as it seems all is suddenly well with the sudden appearance of Sebastian Carruthers, an Englishman visiting the south of France because of a family tale from his grandmother. For Emilie suddenly life is going to be easy and full of light and love. Then everything builds to the top and most highest point of the rollercoaster, emotions are running high and the descent is rather fast and makes her relook at all she has. Does she need to once again reassess all that is left behind?<br /><br />Constance Carruthers is a young married woman, whose husband is missing in action. Not wanting to be idle, Constance goes to do some war work as an office clerk. However, something about Constance stands out and she is one of the few selected to the SOE (Special Operations Executive) and after fierce and extraordinary training she is landed in France, and has to make it to Paris to help the Resistance in Vichy France. However, contact is not easy and she is suddenly all alone in a foregin country, under an assumed name with no hope of ever returning home in the immediate future. It is a case of fight or flight. Constance chooses to fight and finds herself placed in the most extraordinary position in the house of Edouard de la Martinieres. Not how she envisaged spending the war.<br /><br />Here the past and the present collide in Lucinda's story as they have done in her previous novels and is a skill will she handles effectively with ease and no obvious break with the story. Edouard is Emilie's father. Sebastian is Constance's grandson. So the links are complete. All you need to do now is sit back and enjoy the story, it captures you, it shines light in your heart, and it turns the pages long into the night.<br /><br />The author has a skill in drawing you right into the characters lives so much so that you experience all that they do and just as you think you know the outcome or the next stage in their development, it is shifted again. A veritable tease in some ways a good skill of holding the reader's attention in others. I did not want this book to end, it could have been double the size and I still would have wanted to learn more about both the past and the present.<br /><br />If you are looking for a story, perhaps something old fashioned but something with history, romance, big domineering houses that are as good as characters, conflict and resolution, love and loss, prejudice in race, in class then this book will tick all the boxes. Therefore buy it, read it and enjoy it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="627403908178256091" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_354110954" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/354110954" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/546484-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500388520p2/546484.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/354110954?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/546484-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781447218425" href="/book/show/15718885-the-light-behind-the-window">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer354110954" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12998226036067545231">The Light Behind The Window is told in dual-time narrative, a concept that works so well and that Lucinda Riley has mastered excellently. Weaving the modern-day story with the historical background adds a further dimension to the story.<br/><br/>Emilie de la Marinieres finds herself the sole inheritor of a grand chateau in southern France, the death of her Mother has evoked many feelings for her, not all of them good, and many of them very painful. Emilie has always distanced herself from her Mother and h</span>
  <span id="freeText12998226036067545231" style="display:none">The Light Behind The Window is told in dual-time narrative, a concept that works so well and that Lucinda Riley has mastered excellently. Weaving the modern-day story with the historical background adds a further dimension to the story.<br /><br />Emilie de la Marinieres finds herself the sole inheritor of a grand chateau in southern France, the death of her Mother has evoked many feelings for her, not all of them good, and many of them very painful. Emilie has always distanced herself from her Mother and has been living a very ordinary life in Paris. As Emilie begins to sort through her family affairs, she discovers a notebook of poems, written by her Father's sister Sophia. Sophia was never spoken about and is something of a mystery, as Emilie begins to dig deeper into the family secrets she become more and more involved in the past. <br />Back in 1943, Constance Carruthers has been chosen to become part of the Special Operations Executive, she's an ordinary office worker, newly married to a husband who has been missing in action since almost the beginning of the war. After intense training, Constance finds herself in occupied France on a dangerous mission that could cost her her life. <br />Constance finds herself caught up in a complex situation masterminded by Edouard de la Mariniers, and so the connection between the two families begins.<br />Back in the modern day story, Constance's grandson Sebastian has appeared, and he and Emilie become closer and closer. Does Sebastian know more than he is admitting to?<br /><br />I became really emotionally attached to these characters, although I did find Emilie's story a little slow in the beginning, everything soon began to move at a very quick pace and the connections to Constance's war-time story were riveting.<br />Churchill's Special Operations Executive programme was completely new to me, a part of the war that I knew nothing about and I found the details entralling. <br />This novel really is a joy to read, expertly woven together and mixing social history with family dramas and love and relationships - the perfect blend.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12998226036067545231" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2025970264" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16831103413432940108">Started out a bit slow (and silly at times), but developed into an emotional novel that was very engrossing. The suspense was a little on the low side, since the answers to most of the mysteries in the book were quite obvious, but it is still an absorbing read with great characters you'll enjoy rooting for. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_402234390" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/402234390" />
    <a title="Megan Readinginthesunshine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11829532-megan-readinginthesunshine"><img alt="Megan Readinginthesunshine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1396533386p2/11829532.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/402234390?book_show_action=true">Aug 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megan Readinginthesunshine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megan Readinginthesunshine" href="/user/show/11829532-megan-readinginthesunshine">Megan Readinginthesunshine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781447218425" href="/book/show/15718885-the-light-behind-the-window">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer402234390" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5397509233125856157">I was very much looking forward to reading this story, and what a wonderful story it was!!!<br/><br/>The book opens in 1999, with Emilie at her mother’s bedside as she passes away, with Emilie on the brink of inheriting the family estate and fortune. Overwhelmed by all the new decisions Emilie had to make, she runs into Sebastian, a man who has links to the family Château as he says his grandmother, Constance, stayed there during the conflict. As Emilie begins to sort out the family affairs, she begins to</span>
  <span id="freeText5397509233125856157" style="display:none">I was very much looking forward to reading this story, and what a wonderful story it was!!!<br /><br />The book opens in 1999, with Emilie at her mother’s bedside as she passes away, with Emilie on the brink of inheriting the family estate and fortune. Overwhelmed by all the new decisions Emilie had to make, she runs into Sebastian, a man who has links to the family Château as he says his grandmother, Constance, stayed there during the conflict. As Emilie begins to sort out the family affairs, she begins to unlock the family’s deepest secrets and delve into the past. Running alongside this part of the book, we also meet Constance in 1943, a young woman whose husband is missing in action. Constance is selected for the Special Operations Executive, and quickly sent off to France.<br /><br />Lucinda Riley has written a truly captivating tale of love and war. From the moment I picked the story up I became enthralled with it, I simply could not put the book down again. I was spending every chance with my head buried in the pages, keen to find out where the journey would take me next.<br /><br />Lucinda is a very talented author, she effortlessly moves back and forth between the past and the present, cleverly weaving the two times together and creating binding links that ensures the past plays a vital role in shaping the present. I loved every page of the book and was quite sad to finish the story, I must say I feel I gained a lot more knowledge from reading the book, as well as really enjoying the story for what it was.<br /><br />The characters in The Light Behind The Window are exceptional, I became very emotionally involved with them, especially Emilie and Constance. I thought that they were such fantastically written characters. Constance in particular showed such courage and strength in the story and it touched my heart, I really enjoyed reading her part of the story and her journey was a very emotional one. Lucinda Riley has not only created two outstanding main characters, but has excelled in her supporting cast, Sebastian and Alex really stood out for me in that category, not forgetting Sophia as well.<br /><br />I was completely taken in by the story, I loved the story and will be passing it onto my Nan so she can read it (When it arrived in the post she was instantly eyeing it up!). I will definitely be talking and spreading the word about Lucinda’s new novel.<br /><br />The Light Behind The Window takes the reader on an emotional and powerful journey. It is a moving story that had me gripped throughout, and the tale stayed with me long after I had finished reading it. Truly beautiful and captivating.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5397509233125856157" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3568367915" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3568367915" />
    <a title="The Lit Bitch" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4537892-the-lit-bitch"><img alt="The Lit Bitch" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1547250681p2/4537892.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3568367915?book_show_action=true">Oct 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="The Lit Bitch" class="user" itemprop="url" name="The Lit Bitch" href="/user/show/4537892-the-lit-bitch">The Lit Bitch</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3568367915" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13696962992931802037">One night I was browsing for a new audiobook on Audible and the book The Light Behind the Window by Lucinda Riley popped up as a recommended read. I was so excited because I thought it was a new Lucinda Riley book so I downloaded it immediately.<br/><br/>Then I realized that it wasn’t a new Lucinda Riley book but rather the UK title for The Lavender Garden. Which was actually ok because I have had The Lavender Garden on my TBR since 2013 so I thought it must have been a sign that it was time to read it.<br/><br/>I </span>
  <span id="freeText13696962992931802037" style="display:none">One night I was browsing for a new audiobook on Audible and the book The Light Behind the Window by Lucinda Riley popped up as a recommended read. I was so excited because I thought it was a new Lucinda Riley book so I downloaded it immediately.<br /><br />Then I realized that it wasn’t a new Lucinda Riley book but rather the UK title for The Lavender Garden. Which was actually ok because I have had The Lavender Garden on my TBR since 2013 so I thought it must have been a sign that it was time to read it.<br /><br />I started listening to it in my car while driving my son to school one morning and for the rest of the week I found myself leaving the house earlier and earlier to drop him off so that I could listen to this one just a little longer.<br /><br />This book was absolutely stunning and captivating. Did it wrap up a little too neatly and perfectly? Yes of course it did, but did I care at all? No—not even a tiny bit! This book completely captured my attention from the moment I turned it on in my car. It was so good and had everything I expect in a Lucinda Riley book. A sweeping romance/saga, family secrets, and of course elegance. There is just something so posh about Riley and I have yet to read one of her books and feel disappointed—with the exception of The Sun Sister which was only ok for me—every other book has been wonderful.<br /><br />Sure there were moments when I wanted to shake Emilie for all she was worth but I also felt like everything she did fit with her character. She was sheltered and struggled with her own feelings of inadequacy while Sebastian prayed on those. Right from the beginning I did not trust Sebastian. He just felt too convenient but even if the romance between Emilie and Sebastian was wrapped up in the first couple of chapters, Riley has a few tricks and twists up her sleeve when it comes to their romance. I loved how she slowly introduced readers to the idea of another romantic interest for Emilie, it was wonderful to watch unfold in an unexpected way. By the end I was sighing with a big ‘awwwwww’ inside.<br /><br />I will admit I wanted to get back to Emilie’s story more often than Connie’s story. Don’t get me wrong, I thought Connie’s story was rich, well written, and interesting but I felt more of a connection with Emilie. I have read so many books set in WWII or Occupied France with women spies, but I am never tried of hearing their stories, even if they are fictional. I never met a lady WWII spy story that I didn’t like and this one was no exception. I loved Connie and felt her motives and choices aligned with her character as well as the time period. I am not going to ruin it for anyone, but the big decision she makes towards the end of the book just ruined me and broke my heart and I kept waiting for her to change her mind—-but she didn’t. I was so impressed that Riley stayed true to Connie’s character and the time period. The decision would have had repercussions for Connie and even though I wanted her to do the opposite, I felt that it showed the strength of her character and I admired her all the more for it. She felt fully developed and real to me.<br /><br />I adored this book and I just want to reiterate how much I love Lucinda Riley. If you love sweeping sagas with romance and drama this is an author you need to check out. She is truly one of my favorites!<br /><br /><a href="https://thelitbitch.com/2020/10/03/review-the-lavender-garden-by-lucinda-riley-audible-edition/" rel="nofollow noopener">See my full review here</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13696962992931802037" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_421010167" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/421010167" />
    <a title="Jane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2050107-jane"><img alt="Jane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509633087p2/2050107.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/421010167?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jane" href="/user/show/2050107-jane">Jane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781447218425" href="/book/show/15718885-the-light-behind-the-window">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer421010167" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13540893311966629009">I hoped that I would love 'The Light Behind the Window' as much as I loved 'The Girl on the Cliff,' I really did. But I didn't.<br/><br/>There's no doubt at all that you know how to spin a story.<br/><br/>Emilie de la Marinieres travelled from Paris to her family home, a grand chateau in southern France, when she learned that her mother was gravely ill. They hadn't been close: Emilie couldn't understand how her mother found such joy in life as a socialite, and her mother couldn't understand why her daughter had tur</span>
  <span id="freeText13540893311966629009" style="display:none">I hoped that I would love 'The Light Behind the Window' as much as I loved 'The Girl on the Cliff,' I really did. But I didn't.<br /><br />There's no doubt at all that you know how to spin a story.<br /><br />Emilie de la Marinieres travelled from Paris to her family home, a grand chateau in southern France, when she learned that her mother was gravely ill. They hadn't been close: Emilie couldn't understand how her mother found such joy in life as a socialite, and her mother couldn't understand why her daughter had turned her back on all of that, why she wanted a career.<br /><br />Her mother died, and Emilie found that sorting her family affairs would be a huge job, and that she would face difficult and painful decision.<br /><br />And then she met a man. An Englishman. Sebastian Carruthers had just lost his grandmother, the woman who raised him and his brother, and so he could understand her feelings. And he was more than ready to help.<br /><br />Work had brought Sebastian to France, he said, but while he was there he wanted to see that chateau where his grandmother had spent time during the war.<br /><br />In 1943, Constance Carruthers was recruited by the Special Operations Executive, and trained to become an agent. She had family in france, so she spoke the language like a native. And her husband was missing in action; she had to do something, whatever she could to bring the war to an end.<br /><br />Things did not go to plan in France and Constance found herself in the heart of occupied Paris, in the household of Edouard de la Marinieres. Emilie's father.<br /><br />In 1999 Emilie, swept off her feet, married Sebastian. But she didn't get the happy ending she had been hoping for.<br /><br />The story began slowly, and if I hadn't had faith in the author I probably would have given up. The writing was awkward and the dialogue was stilted and weighed down by far too much exposition.<br /><br />But when Connie's story began things picked up. Lucinda Riley's writing is much better when things are happening, and from this point there was plenty happening in both stands of the story. I found that I was reading a book that was both romance and thriller, and that there were so many twists and turns that I had to keep turning the pages to find out what happened.<br /><br />I loved Emilie and Constance; such well drawn characters.<br /><br />The stories of past and present were cleverly, and naturally linked, and it was fascinating to see the one echoing the other. I prefered the wartime story, and though the contemporary story was readable it felt a little bit too contrived, a little bit too hard to believe.<br /><br />There was a lack of subtlety there and in too many other places. The villains in each strand were a particular problem, bit more cartoon baddie than believable human being.<br /><br />Such a pity because there were so many lovely details and wonderful moments.<br /><br />The ending struck a wrong note. It shouldn't have belonged to a former German officer who had concerns about his regime but did nothing more that help those he loved and flee when he feared discovery. Other did far more, risked far more, when they saw the evils of the Nazi regime.<br /><br />There was a better ending there for the taking, and better book to be written from the material.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13540893311966629009" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2660984873" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2660984873" />
    <a title="Chelsea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30098281-chelsea"><img alt="Chelsea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546051703p2/30098281.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2660984873?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea" href="/user/show/30098281-chelsea">Chelsea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2660984873" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5992386023576428528"><u>Impressions</u><br/>This book was fine but ultimately bland. For me, <b>it lacked sparkle, the wow factor </b>of a great book. It is a<b> cheerless read with very few fun or witty lines or moments</b>, so you have to be in the right mood for that. The author does have bursts of talent, as evidenced by nice descriptions like this:<br/><blockquote>"...and gazed out the window at the wisps of cloud suspended like uncooked meringues in the blue sky."</blockquote> but it just doesn't make up for the tedious trudging that defines a good majority of page</span>
  <span id="freeText5992386023576428528" style="display:none"><u>Impressions</u><br />This book was fine but ultimately bland. For me, <b>it lacked sparkle, the wow factor </b>of a great book. It is a<b> cheerless read with very few fun or witty lines or moments</b>, so you have to be in the right mood for that. The author does have bursts of talent, as evidenced by nice descriptions like this:<br /><blockquote>"...and gazed out the window at the wisps of cloud suspended like uncooked meringues in the blue sky."</blockquote> but it just doesn't make up for the tedious trudging that defines a good majority of pages.<br /><br /><u>Irrelevant Title:</u><br />The title of <i>Lavender Garden</i>, or for that matter the UK title of <i>The Light Behind the Window</i>, really had <b>no connection to the novel.</b> I can think of literally a dozen plus alternative titles that would have had more relevance. <br /><br /><u>No big surprises here</u><br />The attempts at <b>twists and plot reveals weren't dramatic. </b>There wasn't much of a character arc for anyone or growth, just further knowledge of someone's story. The author did not make the reader attached to or sympathize with any of the unsavory characters. All of which is<b> fine if you love predictability and 2D characters</b>, so know your preferences. Additionally, there was <b>no difference in voice between Connie and Emilie.</b> <br /><br /><u>Missed opportunities</u><br /><b>Emilie is a vet but we never see that in action</b>. When Frou is dying, she just holds the dog and takes it to...a vet. We don't see her show extra love to animals, why she chose that career (a flashback to having pets because she was lonely growing up thus fueling her ambition for a future career would have been a great touch). She doesn't adopt a pet once she gets a house. She just drops her job she says she loves and... that's it. <b>Dear Lucinda Riley- SHOW, DON'T TELL.</b><br /><br />Connie gets extensively trained as an Ally agent and it basically <b>comes to nothing</b> (she was already a good shot when she was a civilian). I would have loved to see more SOE activity than the very boring accidental "undercover" work. Bland, bland, bland. <br /><br /><u>Content Warnings</u><br /><b>Language:</b> mild/moderate-- a few mild obscenities, an f-word (to be fair, in the intended meaning and uttered by an evil man) and a scatological obscenity <br /><b>Violence: </b>moderate-- war &amp; shootings (not in the battlefield and not gory), a self defensive killing, several deaths <br /><b>Sex/nudity:</b> moderate-- a rape scene that is somewhat detailed, non-descriptive mentions of a married couple kissing and making love, a child is conceived out of wedlock, an unfaithful spouse, infertility discussed <br /><b>Other:</b> name-calling of whore and prostitute, drinking and smoking, mentions of hard drug use <br /><br /><b>Trigger &amp; Age Warning</b><br />Due to the rape scene especially, I would not recommend this to younger teens or those triggered by sexual harassment or rape <br /><br />[spoiler]<br />Why, oh why would someone want to marry the brother of your cheating ex?!? Blegh. Alex could have easily gone with his caretaker he was teaching Russian to and Emilie could have been with the godfather of her now adopted son. You know, her old crush who has loved her for forever that the author totally hinted at but never did anything with? Poor Jean :(</span>
  <a data-text-id="5992386023576428528" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2419628209" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2419628209" />
    <a title="Lynette" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4364138-lynette"><img alt="Lynette" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285973946p2/4364138.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2419628209?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lynette" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lynette" href="/user/show/4364138-lynette">Lynette</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4364138-lynette?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2419628209&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2419628209" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8539429488068107455">This book hit upon nearly all of the things I look for in escapism - old manor houses, the moors, mysterious identities, historical fiction. It was perfect for a rainy day after a long week. I was going to give this a 4-star rating because some of the writing is a bit sloppy and I wasn't thrilled with the plot. Emilie also was difficult to like. She was just so stupid!<br/><br/>But then.<br/><br/>In one of the last chapters, the main character admits that she can't have children, and sobs, "the one thing I believe </span>
  <span id="freeText8539429488068107455" style="display:none">This book hit upon nearly all of the things I look for in escapism - old manor houses, the moors, mysterious identities, historical fiction. It was perfect for a rainy day after a long week. I was going to give this a 4-star rating because some of the writing is a bit sloppy and I wasn't thrilled with the plot. Emilie also was difficult to like. She was just so stupid!<br /><br />But then.<br /><br />In one of the last chapters, the main character admits that she can't have children, and sobs, "the one thing I believe we're put on this earth for, that makes us humans have a point, I cannot fulfill!"<br /><br />Never mind that nowhere up until this point has there been any indication that she wanted child. The thing that bothers me is that AUTHORS KEEP USING THIS AS A DEVICE. It. Is. Tiring. Stop insinuating that a woman's only value is her ability to crap out another human. Stop making women obsess about having children. I swear to god, maybe 85% of the female main characters who are childless HAVING THESE FEELINGS.<br /><br />There are a lot of women out there that don't want children, and for many different reasons. These women lead happy and fulfilling lives. They don't need to push a baby out their vaginas to make a positive contribution to the world.<br /><br />And this made me go from disliking Emilie to loathing her. And to be quite honest, I won't read another book by Riley again. <br /><br />We need more women in these types of stories (i.e. not romance books) who are not only childless, they are content with their childlessness and have no desire to change that, they don't feel their uteruses clench in longing when they see babies, and they aren't magically convinced that all they've ever secretly wanted was to be a mother.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8539429488068107455" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_652693042" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/652693042" />
    <a title="Suzanne Lilly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7238224-suzanne-lilly"><img alt="Suzanne Lilly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1522703437p2/7238224.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/652693042?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Suzanne Lilly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Suzanne Lilly" href="/user/show/7238224-suzanne-lilly">Suzanne Lilly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7238224-suzanne-lilly?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7238224-suzanne-lilly?shelf=women-s-fiction">women-s-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer652693042" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3556382401666647952">With a skilled hand, Lucinda Riley paints a picture of a British woman’s eventful year working as a spy with the French Resistance during World War II. Equally skillfully, she interweaves a story of a modern day French woman faced with the inheritance of a dilapidated estate and hard decisions to make about the chateau and the people who have lived and worked there all their lives.<br/><br/>At first glance, it appears to be a wartime historical novel, but one quickly discovers that Ms. Riley has also delv</span>
  <span id="freeText3556382401666647952" style="display:none">With a skilled hand, Lucinda Riley paints a picture of a British woman’s eventful year working as a spy with the French Resistance during World War II. Equally skillfully, she interweaves a story of a modern day French woman faced with the inheritance of a dilapidated estate and hard decisions to make about the chateau and the people who have lived and worked there all their lives.<br /><br />At first glance, it appears to be a wartime historical novel, but one quickly discovers that Ms. Riley has also delved into the intricacies of the mother-daughter relationship, forbidden love, unrequited love, family heritage and history, and one’s connection with the lands where one is born. Although slightly predictable in its story arc, and with some point of view skips, this novel is still one that is hard to put down. Ms. Riley leads the reader on a great journey, one that brings a new appreciation to the sacrifices made by individuals during the Second World War. It also brings a heightened awareness of the importance of familial ties.<br /><br />As secrets are revealed and motives are uncovered, one becomes more entranced with the characters and how they are all connected. The author has made this common concept enchanting and mesmerizing.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3556382401666647952" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
